# Technical Limits - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Flows

Technical Limits

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Execution Limits](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#execution-limits)
    
*   [File Storage Limits](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#file-storage-limits)
    
*   [Webhook Limits](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#webhook-limits)
    
*   [Key / Value Storage Limits](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#key-%2F-value-storage-limits)
    

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#execution-limits)

Execution Limits

*   **Flow Execution Time**  
    Maximum: **600 seconds (10 minutes)**  
    Flows exceeding this limit will be marked as timed out.
*   **Memory Usage**  
    Maximum: **1 GB RAM**  
    (Self hosted can be configured via `AP_SANDBOX_MEMORY_LIMIT`)

The memory usage is measured for the entire Node.js process running the flow. There is approximately 300 MB of overhead for a warm process with pieces already loaded.

**Note 1:** Flows paused by steps like **Wait for Approval** or **Delay** do **not** count toward the 600-second limit.

**Note 2:** To handle longer processes, split them into multiple flows.  
For example:

*   Have one flow call another via **webhook**.
*   Process smaller **batches of items** in separate flows.

* * *

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#file-storage-limits)

File Storage Limits

Files from actions or triggers are stored in the database/S3 to support retries for certain steps.

*   **Maximum File Size**: **10 MB**  
    (Configurable via `AP_MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB`, default: **25 MB**)
*   **Maximum Flow Run Log Size**: **25 MB**  
    (Configurable via `AP_MAX_FLOW_RUN_LOG_SIZE_MB`, default: **25 MB**)
    
    > This is the total combined size of all inputs and outputs for each step in a single flow run.
    

* * *

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#webhook-limits)

Webhook Limits

*   **Webhook Response Timeout**: **30 seconds** (Configurable via `AP_WEBHOOK_TIMEOUT_SECONDS`, default: **30 seconds**)
    
    > For synchronous webhook requests (URLs ending in `/sync`), Activepieces will wait up to this limit before returning a 408 Request Timeout response.
    
*   **Maximum Webhook Payload Size**: **5 MB** (Configurable via `AP_MAX_WEBHOOK_PAYLOAD_SIZE_MB`, default: **5 MB**)
    
    > Webhook payloads exceeding this limit will be rejected with HTTP 413.
    
*   **Webhook Payload Inline Threshold**: **512 KB** (Configurable via `AP_WEBHOOK_PAYLOAD_INLINE_THRESHOLD_KB`, default: **512 KB**)
    
    > Payloads below this threshold are stored inline in Redis for fastest processing. Payloads above this threshold are offloaded to file storage to protect Redis memory.
    

* * *

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits#key-/-value-storage-limits)

Key / Value Storage Limits

Some pieces use the built-in Activepieces key store (e.g., **Store Piece**, **Queue Piece**).

*   **Maximum Key Length**: **128 characters**
*   **Maximum Value Size**: **512 KB**

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/flows/known-limits.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/flows/known-limits)

[Version History](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/versioning)
[MCP Server](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview)

⌘I

# Build Custom Pieces - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/build-piece#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Misc

Build Custom Pieces

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [How It Works](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/build-piece#how-it-works)
    
*   [Usage](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/build-piece#usage)
    

You can use the CLI to build custom pieces for the platform. This process compiles the pieces and exports them as a `.tgz` packed archive.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/build-piece#how-it-works)

How It Works

The CLI scans the `packages/pieces/` directory for the specified piece. It checks the **name** in the `package.json` file. If the piece is found, it builds and packages it into a `.tgz` archive.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/build-piece#usage)

Usage

To build a piece, follow these steps:

1.  Ensure you have the CLI installed by cloning the repository.
2.  Run the following command:

    npm run build-piece
    

You will be prompted to enter the name of the piece you want to build. For example:

    ? Enter the piece folder name : google-drive
    

The CLI will build the piece and you will be given the path to the archive. For example:

    Piece 'google-drive' built and packed successfully at packages/pieces/community/google-drive/dist
    

You may also build the piece non-interactively by passing the piece name as an argument. For example:

    npm run build-piece google-drive
    

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/misc/build-piece.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/misc/build-piece)

[Piece i18n](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n)
[Publish Custom Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece)

⌘I

# Provision Users - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/provision-users#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Navigation

Essentials

Provision Users

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/provision-users#overview)
    

This feature is available in our paid editions. Contact us [here](https://www.activepieces.com/sales)
, and we'll be delighted to assist you!

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/provision-users#overview)

Overview
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In Activepieces, there are **Projects** and **Users**. Each project is provisioned with their corresponding workspace, project, or team in your SaaS. The users are then mapped to the respective users in Activepieces. To achieve this, the backend will generate a signed token that contains all the necessary information to automatically create a user and project. If the user or project already exists, it will skip the creation and log in the user directly.

1

[](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/provision-users#)

Step 1: Obtain Signing Key

You can generate a signing key by going to **Platform Settings -> Signing Keys -> Generate Signing Key**.This will generate a public and private key pair. The public key will be used by Activepieces to verify the signature of the JWT tokens you send. The private key will be used by you to sign the JWT tokens.![Create Signing Key](https://mintcdn.com/activepieces/ki8mFooo8mAmhMdP/resources/screenshots/create-signing-key.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=ki8mFooo8mAmhMdP&q=85&s=979139e06bf803a368f38dbd356d8d52)

Please store your private key in a safe place, as it will not be stored in Activepieces.

2

[](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/provision-users#)

Step 2: Generate a JWT

The signing key will be used to generate JWT tokens for the currently logged-in user on your website, which will then be sent to the Activepieces Iframe as a query parameter to authenticate the user and exchange the token for a longer lived token.To generate these tokens, you will need to add code in your backend to generate the token using the RS256 algorithm, so the JWT header would look like this:

To obtain the `SIGNING_KEY_ID`, refer to the signing key table and locate the value in the first column.![Signing Key ID](https://mintcdn.com/activepieces/uHZ35vXyxX7goNO-/resources/screenshots/signing-key-id.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=uHZ35vXyxX7goNO-&q=85&s=e4fbadf85aa80f878a53f3e39f6ac591)

    {
      "alg": "RS256",
      "typ": "JWT",
      "kid": "SIGNING_KEY_ID"
    }
    

The signed tokens must include these claims in the payload:

    {
      "version": "v3",
      "externalUserId": "user_id",
      "externalProjectId": "user_project_id",
      "firstName": "John",
      "lastName": "Doe",
      "role": "EDITOR",
      "piecesFilterType": "NONE",
      "exp": 1856563200,
      "tasks": 50000,
      "aiCredits": 250
    }
    

| Claim | Description |
| --- | --- |
| externalUserId | Unique identification of the user in **your** software |
| externalProjectId | Unique identification of the user’s project in **your** software |
| projectDisplayName | Display name of the user’s project |
| firstName | First name of the user |
| lastName | Last name of the user |
| role | Role of the user in the Activepieces project (e.g., **EDITOR**, **VIEWER**, **ADMIN**) |
| exp | Expiry timestamp for the token (Unix timestamp) |
| piecesFilterType | Customize the project pieces, check [customize pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/customize-pieces) |
| piecesTags | Customize the project pieces, check [customize pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/customize-pieces) |
| tasks | Customize the tasks limit for your user’s project |
| aiCredits | Customize the ai credits limit for your user’s project |

You can use any JWT library to generate the token. Here is an example using the jsonwebtoken library in Node.js:

**Friendly Tip #1**: You can also use this [tool](https://dinochiesa.github.io/jwt/)
 to generate a quick example.

**Friendly Tip #2**: Make sure the expiry time is very short, as it’s a temporary token and will be exchanged for a longer-lived token.

Node.js

    const jwt = require('jsonwebtoken');
    
    // JWT NumericDates specified in seconds:
    const currentTime = Math.floor(Date.now() / 1000);
    let token = jwt.sign(
      {
        version: "v3",
        externalUserId: "user_id",
        externalProjectId: "user_project_id",
        firstName: "John",
        lastName: "Doe",
        role: "EDITOR",
        piecesFilterType: "NONE",
        exp: currentTime + (60 * 60), // 1 hour from now
      },
      process.env.ACTIVEPIECES_SIGNING_KEY,
      {
        algorithm: "RS256",
        header: {
          kid: signingKeyID, // Include the "kid" in the header
        },
      }
    );
    

Once you have generated the token, please check the embedding docs to know how to embed the token in the iframe.

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/embedding/provision-users.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/embedding/provision-users)

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Embed Builder](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/embed-builder)

⌘I

# Migrate from Nx to Turbo - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Misc

Migrate from Nx to Turbo

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [What Changed](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#what-changed)
    
*   [Files affected per piece](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#files-affected-per-piece)
    
*   [Automatic Migration](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#automatic-migration)
    
*   [Migrate a specific piece](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#migrate-a-specific-piece)
    
*   [What the script does](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#what-the-script-does)
    
*   [Verify the Migration](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#verify-the-migration)
    

The Activepieces monorepo has fully migrated to Turbo. This guide is kept for **historical reference** and for users with older forks that still use the Nx-based build system.

If you have an existing fork with custom pieces built using the **old Nx-based build system**, you need to migrate them to the new **Turbo-based build system**. This guide explains what changed and provides a migration script.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#what-changed)

What Changed
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Activepieces monorepo replaced [Nx](https://nx.dev/)
 with [Turbo](https://turbo.build/)
 as its build orchestrator. For pieces, this means:

|     | **Old (Nx)** | **New (Turbo)** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Build config | `project.json` per piece | `package.json` scripts |
| Build command | `nx build pieces-{name}` | `turbo run build --filter=@activepieces/piece-{name}` |
| Output directory | `dist/out-tsc` (shared) | `./dist` (local per piece) |
| Task runner | Nx executor (`@nx/js:tsc`) | Direct `tsc -p tsconfig.lib.json && cp package.json dist/` |
| Dependencies | Inferred by Nx graph | Workspace protocol (`workspace:*`) in `package.json` |

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#files-affected-per-piece)

Files affected per piece

*   **`project.json`** — Deleted (no longer needed)
*   **`package.json`** — Added `build` and `lint` scripts, added `main` and `types` fields, added workspace dependencies
*   **`tsconfig.lib.json`** — Updated `outDir`, added `rootDir`, `baseUrl`, `paths`

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#automatic-migration)

Automatic Migration
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Run the migration script to update all custom pieces at once:

    npx ts-node tools/scripts/migrate-custom-piece-to-turbo.ts
    

This scans `packages/pieces/custom/` and applies all necessary changes.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#migrate-a-specific-piece)

Migrate a specific piece

You can also pass a path to migrate a single piece:

    npx ts-node tools/scripts/migrate-custom-piece-to-turbo.ts packages/pieces/custom/my-piece
    

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#what-the-script-does)

What the script does

For each piece, the script:

1.  **Updates `package.json`** — adds `build` and `lint` scripts, sets `main` and `types` entry points, ensures `@activepieces/pieces-framework`, `@activepieces/shared`, and `tslib` are listed as dependencies
2.  **Updates `tsconfig.lib.json`** — sets `outDir` to `./dist`, adds `rootDir`, `baseUrl`, `paths`, and `declaration` settings
3.  **Creates `tsconfig.json`** if missing — extends the root `tsconfig.base.json`
4.  **Deletes `project.json`** — removes Nx configuration

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo#verify-the-migration)

Verify the Migration
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

After migrating, build your piece to verify everything works:

    npx turbo run build --filter=@activepieces/piece-your-piece --force
    

Or use the CLI:

    npm run build-piece your-piece
    

The build output should appear in `packages/pieces/custom/your-piece/dist/`.

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo)

[Custom Pieces CI/CD](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd)
[Setup Private Fork](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/private-fork)

⌘I

# Publish Custom Pieces - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Misc

Publish Custom Pieces

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [How It Works](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece#how-it-works)
    
*   [Usage](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece#usage)
    

You can use the CLI to publish custom pieces to the platform. This process packages the pieces and uploads them to the specified API endpoint.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece#how-it-works)

How It Works

The CLI scans the `packages/pieces/` directory for the specified piece. It checks the **name** and **version** in the `package.json` file. If the piece is not already published, it builds, packages, and uploads it to the platform using the API.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece#usage)

Usage

To publish a piece, follow these steps:

1.  Ensure you have an API Key. Generate it from the Admin Interface by navigating to Settings.
2.  Install the CLI by cloning the repository.
3.  Run the following command:

    npm run publish-piece-to-api
    

4.  You will be asked three questions to publish your piece:

*   `Piece Folder Name`: This is the name associated with the folder where the action resides. It helps organize and categorize actions within the piece.
*   `API URL`: This is the URL of the API endpoint where the piece will be published (ex: [https://cloud.activepieces.com/api](https://cloud.activepieces.com/api)
    ).
*   `API Key Source`: This is the source of the API key. It can be either `Env Variable (AP_API_KEY)` or `Manually`.

In case you choose `Env Variable (AP_API_KEY)`, the CLI will use the API key from the `.env` file in the `packages/server/api` directory. In case you choose `Manually`, you will be asked to enter the API key. Examples:

    npm run publish-piece-to-api
    
    ? Enter the piece folder name : google-drive
    ? Enter the API URL : https://cloud.activepieces.com/api
    ? Enter the API Key Source : Env Variable (AP_API_KEY)
    
    

    npm run publish-piece-to-api
    
    ? Enter the piece folder name : google-drive
    ? Enter the API URL : https://cloud.activepieces.com/api
    ? Enter the API Key Source : Manually
    ? Enter the API Key : ap_1234567890abcdef1234567890abcdef
    
    

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece)

[Build Custom Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/build-piece)
[Custom Pieces CI/CD](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd)

# Custom Pieces CI/CD - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Misc

Custom Pieces CI/CD

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [How It Works](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#how-it-works)
    
*   [Usage](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#usage)
    
*   [Developer Workflow](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#developer-workflow)
    
*   [GitHub Action](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#github-action)
    

You can use the CLI to sync custom pieces. There is no need to rebuild the Docker image as they are loaded directly from npm.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#how-it-works)

How It Works

Use the CLI to sync items from `packages/pieces/custom/` to instances. In production, Activepieces acts as an npm registry, storing all piece versions. The CLI scans the directory for `package.json` files, checking the **name** and **version** of each piece. If a piece isn’t uploaded, it packages and uploads it via the API.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#usage)

Usage

To use the CLI, follow these steps:

1.  Generate an API Key from the Admin Interface. Go to Settings and generate the API Key.
2.  Install the CLI by cloning the repository.
3.  Run the following command, replacing `API_KEY` with your generated API Key and `INSTANCE_URL` with your instance URL:

    AP_API_KEY=your_api_key_here bun run sync-pieces -- --apiUrl https://INSTANCE_URL/api
    

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#developer-workflow)

Developer Workflow

1.  Developers create and modify the pieces offline.
2.  Increment the piece version in their corresponding `package.json`. For more information, refer to the [piece versioning](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning)
     documentation.
3.  Open a pull request towards the main branch.
4.  Once the pull request is merged to the main branch, manually run the CLI or use a GitHub/GitLab Action to trigger the synchronization process.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd#github-action)

GitHub Action

    name: Sync Custom Pieces
    
    on:
      push:
        branches:
          - main
      workflow_dispatch:
    
    jobs:
      sync-pieces:
        runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    
        steps:
          # Step 1: Check out the repository code with full history
          - name: Check out repository code
            uses: actions/checkout@v3
            with:
              fetch-depth: 0
    
          # Step 2: Set up Bun
          - name: Set up Bun
            uses: oven-sh/setup-bun@v1
            with:
              bun-version: latest
    
          # Step 3: Cache Bun dependencies
          - name: Cache Bun dependencies
            uses: actions/cache@v3
            with:
              path: ~/.bun/install/cache
              key: bun-${{ hashFiles('bun.lockb') }}
              restore-keys: |
                bun-
    
          # Step 4: Install dependencies using Bun
          - name: Install dependencies
            run: bun install --no-save
    
          # Step 5: Sync Custom Pieces
          - name: Sync Custom Pieces
            env:
              AP_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.AP_API_KEY }}
            run: bun run sync-pieces -- --apiUrl ${{ secrets.INSTANCE_URL }}/api
    
    

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/misc/pieces-ci-cd)

[Publish Custom Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/publish-piece)
[Migrate from Nx to Turbo](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo)

[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Stop Flow](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control#stop-flow)
    
*   [Pause Flow and Wait for Webhook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control#pause-flow-and-wait-for-webhook)
    
*   [Pause Flow and Delay](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control#pause-flow-and-delay)
    

Flow Controls provide the ability to control the flow of execution from inside a piece. By using the `ctx` parameter in the `run` method of actions, you can perform various operations to control the flow.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control#stop-flow)

Stop Flow
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can stop the flow and provide a response to the webhook trigger. This can be useful when you want to terminate the execution of the piece and send a specific response back. **Example with Response:**

    context.run.stop({
      response: {
        status: context.propsValue.status ?? StatusCodes.OK,
        body: context.propsValue.body,
        headers: (context.propsValue.headers as Record<string, string>) ?? {},
      },
    });
    

**Example without Response:**

    context.run.stop();
    

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control#pause-flow-and-wait-for-webhook)

Pause Flow and Wait for Webhook
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can pause flow and return HTTP response, also provide a callback to URL that you can call with certain payload and continue the flow. **Example:**

    ctx.run.pause({
      pauseMetadata: {
        type: PauseType.WEBHOOK,
        response: {
          callbackUrl: context.generateResumeUrl({
            queryParams: {},
          }),
        },
      },
    });
    

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control#pause-flow-and-delay)

Pause Flow and Delay
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can pause or delay the flow until a specific timestamp. Currently, the only supported type of pause is a delay based on a future timestamp. **Example:**

    ctx.run.pause({
        pauseMetadata: {
            type: PauseType.DELAY,
            resumeDateTime: futureTime.toUTCString()
        }
    });
    

These flow hooks give you control over the execution of the piece by allowing you to stop the flow or pause it until a certain condition is met. You can use these hooks to customize the behavior and flow of your actions.

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control)

[Props Validation](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/properties-validation)
[Persistent Storage](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage)

⌘I

🔥 Why Activepieces is Different:
===========================================================================================================================

*   **💖 Loved by Everyone**: Intuitive interface and great experience for both technical and non-technical users with a quick learning curve.

![](https://mintcdn.com/activepieces/uHZ35vXyxX7goNO-/resources/templates.gif?s=076362bc114929ee518e20251d901b17)

*   **🌐 Open Ecosystem:** All pieces are open source and available on npmjs.com, **60% of the pieces are contributed by the community**.
*   **🛠️ Pieces are written in Typescript**: Pieces are npm packages in TypeScript, offering full customization with the best developer experience, including **hot reloading** for **local** piece development on your machine. 😎

![](https://mintcdn.com/activepieces/ki8mFooo8mAmhMdP/resources/create-action.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=ki8mFooo8mAmhMdP&q=85&s=fb6b48d36b7deb67a7ba801a6780a8b6)

*   **🤖 AI-Ready**: Native AI pieces and agents are built into Activepieces. Integrating AI into your flows is seamless and simple—experiment with popular providers, or quickly create custom agents using our easy-to-use AI SDK.
*   **🏢 Enterprise-Ready**: Developers set up the tools, and anyone in the organization can use the no-code builder. Full customization from branding to control.
*   **🔒 Secure by Design**: Self-hosted and network-gapped for maximum security and control over your data.
*   **🧠 Human in Loop**: Delay execution for a period of time or require approval. These are just pieces built on top of the piece framework, and you can build many pieces like that. 🎨

# Enable Custom API Calls - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/custom-api-calls#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Piece Reference

Enable Custom API Calls

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Basic Example](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/custom-api-calls#basic-example)
    
*   [Dynamic Base URL and Basic Auth Example](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/custom-api-calls#dynamic-base-url-and-basic-auth-example)
    

Custom API Calls allow the user to send a request to a specific endpoint if no action has been implemented for it. This will show in the actions list of the piece as `Custom API Call`, to enable this action for a piece, you need to call the `createCustomApiCallAction` in your actions array.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/custom-api-calls#basic-example)

Basic Example
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The example below implements the action for the OpenAI piece. The OpenAI piece uses a `Bearer token` authorization header to identify the user sending the request.

    actions: [\
      ...yourActions,\
      createCustomApiCallAction({\
        // The auth object defined in the piece\
        auth: openaiAuth,\
        // The base URL for the API\
        baseUrl: () => {\
          'https://api.openai.com/v1'\
        },\
        // Mapping the auth object to the needed authorization headers\
        authMapping: async (auth) => {\
          return {\
            'Authorization': `Bearer ${auth}`\
          }\
        }\
      })\
    ]
    

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/custom-api-calls#dynamic-base-url-and-basic-auth-example)

Dynamic Base URL and Basic Auth Example
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The example below implements the action for the Jira Cloud piece. The Jira Cloud piece uses a dynamic base URL for it’s actions, where the base URL changes based on the values the user authenticated with. We will also implement a Basic authentication header.

    actions: [\
      ...yourActions,\
      createCustomApiCallAction({\
        baseUrl: (auth) => {\
          return `${(auth as JiraAuth).instanceUrl}/rest/api/3`\
        },\
        auth: jiraCloudAuth,\
        authMapping: async (auth) => {\
          const typedAuth = auth  as JiraAuth\
          return {\
            'Authorization': `Basic ${typedAuth.email}:${typedAuth.apiToken}`\
          }\
        }\
      })\
    ]
    

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/custom-api-calls.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/piece-reference/custom-api-calls)

[Piece Examples](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/examples)
[Piece i18n](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n)

⌘I

# Setup Private Fork - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/private-fork#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Misc

Setup Private Fork

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Create a Private Fork (Private Pieces)](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/private-fork#create-a-private-fork-private-pieces)
    
*   [Sync Your Fork](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/private-fork#sync-your-fork)
    

**Friendly Tip #1:** If you want to experiment, you can fork or clone the public repository.

For private piece installation, you will need the paid edition. However, you can still develop pieces, contribute them back, **OR** publish them to the public npm registry and use them in your own instance or project.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/private-fork#create-a-private-fork-private-pieces)

Create a Private Fork (Private Pieces)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By following these steps, you can create a private fork on GitHub, GitLab or another platform and configure the “activepieces” repository as the upstream source, allowing you to incorporate changes from the “activepieces” repository.

1.  **Clone the Repository:**

Begin by creating a bare clone of the repository. Remember that this is a temporary step and will be deleted later.

    git clone --bare [email protected]:activepieces/activepieces.git
    

2.  **Create a Private Git Repository**

Generate a new private repository on GitHub or your chosen platform. When initializing the new repository, do not include a README, license, or gitignore files. This precaution is essential to avoid merge conflicts when synchronizing your fork with the original repository.

3.  **Mirror-Push to the Private Repository:**

Mirror-push the bare clone you created earlier to your newly created “activepieces” repository. Make sure to replace `<your_username>` in the URL below with your actual GitHub username.

    cd activepieces.git
    git push --mirror [email protected]:<your_username>/activepieces.git
    

4.  **Remove the Temporary Local Repository:**

    cd ..
    rm -rf activepieces.git
    

5.  **Clone Your Private Repository:**

Now, you can clone your “activepieces” repository onto your local machine into your desired directory.

    cd ~/path/to/directory
    git clone [email protected]:<your_username>/activepieces.git
    

6.  **Add the Original Repository as a Remote:**

If desired, you can add the original repository as a remote to fetch potential future changes. However, remember to disable push operations for this remote, as you are not permitted to push changes to it.

    git remote add upstream [email protected]:activepieces/activepieces.git
    git remote set-url --push upstream DISABLE
    

You can view a list of all your remotes using `git remote -v`. It should resemble the following:

    origin	[email protected]:<your_username>/activepieces.git (fetch)
    origin	[email protected]:<your_username>/activepieces.git (push)
    upstream	[email protected]:activepieces/activepieces.git (fetch)
    upstream	DISABLE (push)
    

> When pushing changes, always use `git push origin`.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/private-fork#sync-your-fork)

Sync Your Fork

To retrieve changes from the “upstream” repository, fetch the remote and rebase your work on top of it.

    git fetch upstream
    git merge upstream/main
    

Conflict resolution should not be necessary since you’ve only added pieces to your repository.

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/misc/private-fork.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/misc/private-fork)

[Migrate from Nx to Turbo](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/migrate-nx-to-turbo)
[Testing Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces)

⌘I

# Testing Pieces - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Misc

Testing Pieces

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Setup](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#setup)
    
*   [1\. Add vitest to your piece](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#1-add-vitest-to-your-piece)
    
*   [2\. Create a vitest config](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#2-create-a-vitest-config)
    
*   [3\. Write tests](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#3-write-tests)
    
*   [4\. Run tests](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#4-run-tests)
    

Testing pieces is **optional** but recommended for complex logic. Pieces can be tested using [Vitest](https://vitest.dev/)
 with the `createMockActionContext` helper from the framework. For a full working example, see the [text-helper piece tests on GitHub](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/tree/main/packages/pieces/core/text-helper/test)
.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#setup)

Setup
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#1-add-vitest-to-your-piece)

1\. Add vitest to your piece

Add `vitest` as a dev dependency in your piece’s `package.json` and add a `test` script:

    {
      "scripts": {
        "build": "tsc -p tsconfig.lib.json && cp package.json dist/",
        "lint": "eslint 'src/**/*.ts'",
        "test": "vitest run"
      },
      "devDependencies": {
        "vitest": "3.0.8"
      }
    }
    

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#2-create-a-vitest-config)

2\. Create a vitest config

Create `vitest.config.ts` in your piece root:

    import path from 'path'
    import { defineConfig } from 'vitest/config'
    
    const repoRoot = path.resolve(__dirname, '../../../..')
    
    export default defineConfig({
      test: {
        globals: true,
        environment: 'node',
      },
      resolve: {
        alias: {
          '@activepieces/shared': path.resolve(repoRoot, 'packages/shared/src/index.ts'),
          '@activepieces/pieces-framework': path.resolve(repoRoot, 'packages/pieces/framework/src/index.ts'),
          '@activepieces/pieces-common': path.resolve(repoRoot, 'packages/pieces/common/src/index.ts'),
        },
      },
    })
    

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#3-write-tests)

3\. Write tests

Create a `test/` directory and add `.test.ts` files:

    import { createMockActionContext } from '@activepieces/pieces-framework';
    import { myAction } from '../src/lib/actions/my-action';
    
    describe('myAction', () => {
      test('does something', async () => {
        const ctx = createMockActionContext({
          propsValue: {
            inputField: 'test value',
          },
        });
    
        const result = await myAction.run(ctx);
        expect(result).toBe('expected output');
      });
    });
    

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces#4-run-tests)

4\. Run tests

    # Run tests for a specific piece
    npx turbo test --filter=@activepieces/piece-text-helper
    
    # Run tests directly from the piece directory
    cd packages/pieces/core/text-helper
    npx vitest run
    

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/misc/testing-pieces)

[Setup Private Fork](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/private-fork)
[Dev Containers](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/misc/dev-container)

⌘I

# Files - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/files#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Piece Reference

Files

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Write](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/files#write)
    

The `ctx.files` object allow you to store files in local storage or in a remote storage depending on the run environment.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/files#write)

Write
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can use the `write` method to write a file to the storage, It returns a string that can be used in other actions or triggers properties to reference the file. **Example:**

    const fileReference = await files.write({
        fileName: 'file.txt',
        data: Buffer.from('text')
    });
    

This code will store the file in the database If the run environment is testing mode since it will be required to test other steps, other wise it will store it in the local temporary directory.

For Reading the file If you are using the file property in a trigger or action, It will be automatically parsed and you can use it directly, please refer to `Property.File` in the [properties](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/properties#file)
 section.

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/files.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/piece-reference/files)

[Persistent Storage](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage)
[External Libraries](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/external-libraries)

# Piece i18n - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Piece Reference

Piece i18n

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

1

[](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n#)

Generate

Run the following command to create a translation file with all the strings that need translation in your piece

    npm run cli pieces generate-translation-file PIECE_FOLDER_NAME
    

2

[](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n#)

Translate

Make a copy of `packages/pieces/<community_or_custom>/<your_piece>/src/i18n/translation.json`, name it `<locale>.json` i.e fr.json and translate the values.

For open source pieces, you can use the [Crowdin project](https://crowdin.com/project/activepieces)
 to translate to different languages. These translations will automatically sync back to your code.

3

[](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n#)

Test Locally

After following the steps to [setup your development environment](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/development-setup)
, click the small cog icon next to the logo in your dashboard and change the locale.![Locales](https://mintcdn.com/activepieces/ki8mFooo8mAmhMdP/resources/i18n-pieces.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=ki8mFooo8mAmhMdP&q=85&s=81406211f34fd0ec06e761005fc759ca)  
In the builder your piece will now appear in the translated language:![French Webhooks](https://mintcdn.com/activepieces/ki8mFooo8mAmhMdP/resources/french-webhooks.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=ki8mFooo8mAmhMdP&q=85&s=fcf11162f3e2554ff16e1e728cfb25f6)

4

[](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n#)

Publish

Follow the docs here to [publish your piece](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/sharing-pieces/overview)

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/piece-reference/i18n)

[Enable Custom API Calls](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/custom-api-calls)

On this page

*   [Semantic Versioning](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#semantic-versioning)
    
*   [Engine](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#engine)
    
*   [Examples](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#examples)
    
*   [Breaking changes](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#breaking-changes)
    
*   [Non-breaking changes](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#non-breaking-changes)
    

Pieces are npm packages and follows **semantic versioning**.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#semantic-versioning)

Semantic Versioning
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The version number consists of three numbers: `MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH`, where:

*   **MAJOR** It should be incremented when there are breaking changes to the piece.
*   **MINOR** It should be incremented for new features or functionality that is compatible with the previous version, unless the major version is less than 1.0, in which case it can be a breaking change.
*   **PATCH** It should be incremented for bug fixes and small changes that do not introduce new features or break backward compatibility.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#engine)

Engine
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The engine will use the most up-to-date compatible version for a given piece version during the **DRAFT** flow versions. Once the flow is published, all pieces will be locked to a specific version. **Case 1: Piece Version is Less Than 1.0**: The engine will select the latest **patch** version that shares the same **minor** version number. **Case 2: Piece Version Reaches Version 1.0**: The engine will select the latest **minor** version that shares the same **major** version number.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#examples)

Examples
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

when you make a change, remember to increment the version accordingly.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#breaking-changes)

Breaking changes

*   Remove an existing action.
*   Add a required `action` prop.
*   Remove an existing action prop, whether required or optional.
*   Remove an attribute from an action output.
*   Change the existing behavior of an action/trigger.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning#non-breaking-changes)

Non-breaking changes

*   Add a new action.
*   Add an optional `action` prop.
*   Add an attribute to an action output.

i.e., any removal is breaking, any required addition is breaking, everything else is not breaking.

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/piece-reference/piece-versioning)

[External Libraries](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/external-libraries)
[Piece Examples](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/examples)

⌘I

# Persistent Storage - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Piece Reference

Persistent Storage

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Put](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage#put)
    
*   [Get](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage#get)
    
*   [Delete](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage#delete)
    

The `ctx` parameter inside triggers and actions provides a simple key/value storage mechanism. The storage is persistent, meaning that the stored values are retained even after the execution of the piece. By default, the storage operates at the flow level, but it can also be configured to store values at the project level.

The storage scope is completely isolated. If a key is stored in a different scope, it will not be fetched when requested in different scope.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage#put)

Put
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can store a value with a specified key in the storage. **Example:**

    ctx.store.put('KEY', 'VALUE', StoreScope.PROJECT);
    

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage#get)

Get
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can retrieve the value associated with a specific key from the storage. **Example:**

    const value = ctx.store.get<string>('KEY', StoreScope.PROJECT);
    

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage#delete)

Delete
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can delete a key-value pair from the storage. **Example:**

    ctx.store.delete('KEY', StoreScope.PROJECT);
    

These storage operations allow you to store, retrieve, and delete key-value pairs in the persistent storage. You can use this storage mechanism to store and retrieve data as needed within your triggers and actions.

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/piece-reference/persistent-storage)

[Flow Control](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/flow-control)
[Files](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/files)

⌘I

# Create Action - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Build a Piece

Create Action

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [Action Definition](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action#action-definition)
    
*   [Expose The Definition](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action#expose-the-definition)
    
*   [Testing](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action#testing)
    

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action#action-definition)

Action Definition
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Now let’s create first action which fetch random ice-cream flavor.

    npm run cli actions create
    

You will be asked three questions to define your new piece:

1.  `Piece Folder Name`: This is the name associated with the folder where the action resides. It helps organize and categorize actions within the piece.
2.  `Action Display Name`: The name users see in the interface, conveying the action’s purpose clearly.
3.  `Action Description`: A brief, informative text in the UI, guiding users about the action’s function and purpose. Next, let’s create the action file:

**Example:**

    npm run cli actions create
    
    ? Enter the piece folder name : gelato
    ? Enter the action display name : get icecream flavor
    ? Enter the action description : fetches random icecream flavor.
    

This will create a new TypeScript file named `get-icecream-flavor.ts` in the `packages/pieces/community/gelato/src/lib/actions` directory. Inside this file, paste the following code:

    import {
      createAction,
      Property,
      PieceAuth,
    } from '@activepieces/pieces-framework';
    import { httpClient, HttpMethod } from '@activepieces/pieces-common';
    import { gelatoAuth } from '../..';
    
    export const getIcecreamFlavor = createAction({
      name: 'get_icecream_flavor', // Must be a unique across the piece, this shouldn't be changed.
      auth: gelatoAuth,
      displayName: 'Get Icecream Flavor',
      description: 'Fetches random icecream flavor',
      props: {},
      async run(context) {
        const res = await httpClient.sendRequest<string[]>({
          method: HttpMethod.GET,
          url: 'https://cloud.activepieces.com/api/v1/webhooks/RGjv57ex3RAHOgs0YK6Ja/sync',
          headers: {
            Authorization: context.auth, // Pass API key in headers
          },
        });
        return res.body;
      },
    });
    

The createAction function takes an object with several properties, including the `name`, `displayName`, `description`, `props`, and `run` function of the action. The `name` property is a unique identifier for the action. The `displayName` and `description` properties are used to provide a human-readable name and description for the action. The `props` property is an object that defines the properties that the action requires from the user. In this case, the action doesn’t require any properties. The `run` function is the function that is called when the action is executed. It takes a single argument, context, which contains the values of the action’s properties. The `run` function utilizes the httpClient.sendRequest function to make a GET request, fetching a random ice cream flavor. It incorporates API key authentication in the request headers. Finally, it returns the response body.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action#expose-the-definition)

Expose The Definition
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To make the action readable by Activepieces, add it to the array of actions in the piece definition.

    import { createPiece } from '@activepieces/pieces-framework';
    // Don't forget to add the following import.
    import { getIcecreamFlavor } from './lib/actions/get-icecream-flavor';
    
    export const gelato = createPiece({
      displayName: 'Gelato',
      logoUrl: 'https://cdn.activepieces.com/pieces/gelato.png',
      authors: [],
      auth: gelatoAuth,
      // Add the action here.
      actions: [getIcecreamFlavor], // <--------
      triggers: [],
    });
    

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action#testing)

Testing
====================================================================================================

By default, the development setup only builds specific components. Open the file `.env.dev` and include “gelato” in the `AP_DEV_PIECES`. For more details, check out the [Piece Development](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/development-setup#pieces-development)
 section. Once you edit the environment variable, restart the backend. The piece will be rebuilt. After this process, you’ll need to **refresh** the frontend to see the changes.

If the build fails, try debugging by running `npx turbo run build --filter=@activepieces/piece-gelato`. It will display any errors in your code.

To test the action, use the flow builder in Activepieces. It should function as shown in the screenshot. ![Gelato Action](https://mintcdn.com/activepieces/uHZ35vXyxX7goNO-/resources/screenshots/gelato-action.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=uHZ35vXyxX7goNO-&q=85&s=799c7211ce7bdc240960f0e15c1ac76c)

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-action)

[Add Piece Authentication](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/piece-authentication)
[Create Trigger](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/create-trigger)

⌘I

# Props Validation - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/properties-validation#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Piece Reference

Props Validation

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

Activepieces uses Zod for runtime validation of piece properties. Zod provides a powerful schema validation system that helps ensure your piece receives valid inputs. To use Zod validation in your piece, first import the validation helper and Zod:

Please make sure the `minimumSupportedRelease` is set to at least `0.36.1` for the validation to work.

    import { createAction, Property } from '@activepieces/pieces-framework';
    import { propsValidation } from '@activepieces/pieces-common';
    import { z } from 'zod';
    
    export const getIcecreamFlavor = createAction({
      name: 'get_icecream_flavor', // Unique name for the action.
      displayName: 'Get Ice Cream Flavor',
      description: 'Fetches a random ice cream flavor based on user preferences.',
      props: {
        sweetnessLevel: Property.Number({
          displayName: 'Sweetness Level',
          required: true,
          description: 'Specify the sweetness level (0 to 10).',
        }),
        includeToppings: Property.Checkbox({
          displayName: 'Include Toppings',
          required: false,
          description: 'Should the flavor include toppings?',
          defaultValue: true,
        }),
        numberOfFlavors: Property.Number({
          displayName: 'Number of Flavors',
          required: true,
          description: 'How many flavors do you want to fetch? (1-5)',
          defaultValue: 1,
        }),
      },
      async run({ propsValue }) {
        // Validate the input properties using Zod
        await propsValidation.validateZod(propsValue, {
          sweetnessLevel: z.number().min(0).max(10, 'Sweetness level must be between 0 and 10.'),
          numberOfFlavors: z.number().min(1).max(5, 'You can fetch between 1 and 5 flavors.'),
        });
    
        // Action logic
        const sweetnessLevel = propsValue.sweetnessLevel;
        const includeToppings = propsValue.includeToppings ?? true; // Default to true
        const numberOfFlavors = propsValue.numberOfFlavors;
    
        // Simulate fetching random ice cream flavors
        const allFlavors = [\
          'Vanilla',\
          'Chocolate',\
          'Strawberry',\
          'Mint',\
          'Cookie Dough',\
          'Pistachio',\
          'Mango',\
          'Coffee',\
          'Salted Caramel',\
          'Blackberry',\
        ];
        const selectedFlavors = allFlavors.slice(0, numberOfFlavors);
    
        return {
          message: `Here are your ${numberOfFlavors} flavors: ${selectedFlavors.join(', ')}`,
          sweetnessLevel: sweetnessLevel,
          includeToppings: includeToppings,
        };
      },
    });
    
    

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/build-pieces/piece-reference/properties-validation.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/build-pieces/piece-reference/properties-validation)

# MCP Server - Activepieces

[Skip to main content](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#content-area)

[Activepieces home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/activepieces/resources/logo/dark.svg)](https://www.activepieces.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

MCP Server

MCP Server

[Overview](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/overview/welcome)
[Admin Guide](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/admin-guide/guides/structure-projects)
[Deploy](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/install/overview)
[Embedding](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/embedding/overview)
[Build Pieces](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/build-pieces/building-pieces/overview)
[API Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/endpoints/overview)
[Handbook](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/handbook/overview)

On this page

*   [What is MCP?](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#what-is-mcp)
    
*   [Enable the MCP Server](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#enable-the-mcp-server)
    
*   [Connect Your AI Assistant](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#connect-your-ai-assistant)
    
*   [Claude Desktop](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#claude-desktop)
    
*   [Cursor / Other MCP Clients](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#cursor-%2F-other-mcp-clients)
    
*   [Tool Categories](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#tool-categories)
    
*   [Security](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#security)
    

Activepieces includes a built-in MCP server that allows AI assistants (Claude, GPT, etc.) to interact with your automation platform. AI agents can build flows, manage tables, test automations, and more — all through natural language.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#what-is-mcp)

What is MCP?
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The [Model Context Protocol](https://modelcontextprotocol.io/)
 is an open standard that lets AI assistants connect to external tools and data sources. Activepieces implements an MCP server that exposes 30 tools for managing your automation workflows.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#enable-the-mcp-server)

Enable the MCP Server
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Go to **Settings** → **MCP Server**
2.  Toggle the server **on**
3.  Copy the **server URL** and **token**

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#connect-your-ai-assistant)

Connect Your AI Assistant
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The MCP server uses the **Streamable HTTP** transport. Configure your AI client with:

*   **URL**: `https://your-instance.com/api/v1/projects/{projectId}/mcp-server/http`
*   **Authentication**: Bearer token (or `?token=` query parameter)

The token can be rotated at any time from the MCP Server settings page.

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#claude-desktop)

Claude Desktop

Add this to your Claude Desktop config (`claude_desktop_config.json`):

    {
      "mcpServers": {
        "activepieces": {
          "url": "https://your-instance.com/api/v1/projects/{projectId}/mcp-server/http?token={your-token}"
        }
      }
    }
    

### 

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#cursor-/-other-mcp-clients)

Cursor / Other MCP Clients

Use the Streamable HTTP URL with your token as a Bearer token in the Authorization header.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#tool-categories)

Tool Categories
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Tools are organized into categories. **Discovery tools** are always available. Other categories can be enabled or disabled per-project in the MCP Server settings.

| Category | Tools | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| [Discovery](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#discovery) | 10  | Read-only tools for exploring flows, pieces, tables, runs, and AI models |
| [Flow Management](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#flow-management) | 4   | Create, rename, publish, and enable/disable flows |
| [Flow Building](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#flow-building) | 4   | Add, update, and delete steps and triggers |
| [Router & Branching](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#router-branching) | 2   | Add and delete conditional branches |
| [Annotations](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#annotations) | 1   | Manage canvas notes |
| [Tables](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#tables) | 6   | Full CRUD for tables, fields, and records |
| [Testing & Runs](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#testing-runs) | 3   | Test flows, inspect results, retry failures |

See the [Tools Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/tools)
 for the complete catalog with input schemas and examples.

[​](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/overview#security)

Security
------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Credentials are never exposed** — connection secrets, API keys, and OAuth tokens are never returned by any MCP tool
*   **Project-scoped** — all operations are scoped to the authenticated project
*   **Sensitive setup** — the `ap_setup_guide` tool returns instructions for the user to configure connections and AI providers in the UI, rather than handling secrets through MCP
*   **Token rotation** — the MCP token can be rotated at any time without affecting existing connections or flows

[Suggest edits](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/edit/main/docs/mcp/overview.mdx)
[Raise issue](https://github.com/activepieces/activepieces/issues/new?title=Issue%20on%20docs&body=Path:%20/mcp/overview)

[Technical Limits](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/flows/known-limits)
[Tools Reference](https://www.activepieces.com/docs/mcp/tools)

⌘I
